International Olympic Committee Passes Locations for the Next Three Meetings

Requests All Countries Not to Award Cash Prizes to Athletes

(Havas Agency, Oslo, 1st) The International Olympic Committee has recently decided that the next three meetings will be held in Berlin in 1936, Warsaw in 1937, and Cairo, Egypt in 1938. The committee, having heard that some countries intend to award cash prizes to the winners, discussed this matter especially today. It was decided to request that the Olympic Committees of all countries not implement this fact, as athletes will lose their amateur status once they accept cash. Regarding the location of the 1940 Olympic Games, the Italian representative did withdraw the request to hold them in Rome at today's meeting, but the situation is still chaotic, as representatives of most of the non-attending countries have already voted, and some of them must have voted for Italy. The chairman of the International Olympic Committee, Belgian representative Berela, did not want the committee's decision to be seen as a political compromise, and proposed to postpone the decision on the location of the 1940 Olympic Games until the International Committee meets in Berlin next year. All the committee members, except for the representative of one country who abstained, expressed their approval, and this proposal was finally passed.

Industry and Commerce Soccer Match, Municipal and Earth Team Wins Championship

Team Match Results

Movement and Protection beats Shun Kee, 3 to 2

Construction and Earth beats Construction Nation, 2 to 1

Construction and China beats Asia, 1 to 0

China beats South Light and One Heart, 1 to 1

The Movement and Protection and Shun Kee teams in the Movement group were both strong teams. Since the beginning of the competition, neither had been defeated, creating a standoff. Although Movement and Protection still has one game to play, judging by the usual situation, their championship position is unlikely to change. Based on yesterday's match, Shun Kee's defense was stronger, and they had more opportunities to shoot, but the god of soccer did not favor them, and they missed by a hair's breadth each time. They lost their previous achievements by a single goal, which is a pity.

The Municipal and Earth team in the Construction group has four wins and one draw to date. Construction Nation had four wins. Yesterday's encounter was a battle for dominance. The first half ended in a 1-1 tie. In the second half, the Municipal and Earth team scored again, while Construction Nation made no progress. Therefore, the Municipal and Earth team won 2-1, securing the championship for their group, because the Municipal and Earth team has completed all their matches, and the other teams' scores are not as high as the Municipal and Earth team.

Many members of the Yi Zhong team in the Student group cannot take time off to attend matches on Saturdays and Sundays due to work commitments. They have forfeited several matches in a row and feel that this is detrimental to the spirit of the competition, so they have sent a letter to the association requesting to withdraw. From now on, teams scheduled to play against Yi Zhong in that group do not need to appear.

(Central News Agency, Lanzhou, 1st) Gansu Chairman Zhu Shaoliang recently telegraphed the Ministry of Finance stating that since the abolition of harsh taxes and levies in the province, fiscal revenue has decreased sharply. Establishment of the Bio-Statistical Laboratory of the Institute of History and Philology of the Academia Sinica

The Fourth Group of the Institute of History and Philology of the National Academia Sinica was reorganized and established last summer as the only national institution dedicated to the study of biostatistics, anthropology, and ethnology. Researchers Ling Chunsheng and Tao Yunkui of the group, at the invitation of the Yunnan Provincial Government, went to Yunnan last autumn to conduct field work. The group's overall plan is headed by Dr. Wu Dingliang, who returned to China from Europe at the end of last year and began preparations. Recently, two laboratories have been established: (1) a statistical laboratory equipped with various calculators and mathematical drawing instruments; (2) an anthropology laboratory divided into two parts: A, measuring various bones; B, measuring the human body. Various measuring instruments are extremely complete, and some are newly manufactured according to the latest European styles. Dr. Wu has completed the planning of the following four research projects: (1) comparison of exponential distribution curves; (2) relationship between lifespan and number of descendants (based on genealogical research and actual surveys); (3) research on the physique and characteristics of people in Jiangsu and Zhejiang; (4) research on skulls and long bones from the Sui and Tang dynasties (in collaboration with Mr. Li Ji). The first two research projects are in the field of statistics, and the latter two are in the field of anthropology. All have now begun, and it is hoped that they will be completed in the shortest possible time.

Jiangxi Province Implements Compulsory Literacy

The period from April this year to April next year is designated as the Popular Education Movement Year

(Nanchang, 2nd) After the bandits in Jiangxi Province have been cleared, popular education is particularly important. The Department of Education has designated the period from April this year to April next year as the Popular Education Movement Year to eliminate illiteracy. Men aged sixteen to fifty must be forced to become literate. Those who are literate have the obligation to teach. People in the education sector are mobilized to take on teaching work.

The Central Library is About to be Constructed

The preparatory office of the National Central Library previously requested the Ministry of Education to allocate a site for construction. The Ministry of Education, based on the situation, consulted the Beijing Municipal Government to allocate land. According to news from the library, the land has been allocated by the Beijing Municipal Government, and the 80 mu of empty land in the Forbidden City is connected to the construction site of the Central Committee. The library has already drawn up plans for the construction of the building. However, although the construction project is expected to be completed in two years, the construction funds, 1.5 million yuan allocated from 10% of the interest from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund, will only allocate 150,000 yuan in the 23rd year, which is difficult to apply. In addition, borrowing from banks would incur considerable interest expenses. It is reported that other methods are being considered for construction costs. Once a solution to the funding problem is found, preparations for the construction of the building will begin.

China Cultural Construction Association Organizes Reading Advancement Association

Preparations are Complete, and Reward Methods Have Been Determined

Chen Lifu, Cai Yuanpei, and Others Hired as Book Selection Committee Members

The First Phase of Reading Methods Will Be Officially Announced Soon

The initiation of a reading movement by Wu Xingya and Pan Gongzhan of the China Cultural Construction Association was reported in the previous issue. It is now reported that the preparatory committee of the Reading Advancement Association organized by the association has been established and has held two meetings, passed simple regulations, determined the reward methods, and drafted a list of book review committee members. Once the review committee members select the books, the first phase of the book list will be officially announced. The process and simple regulations are recorded separately below.

Preparation Process

At 6:00 PM on the 24th of last month, Wu Xingya convened a discussion meeting at the Dongya Restaurant to exchange opinions on the organization of a reading association. The participants agreed that it was necessary to establish a preparatory committee. Wu Xingya was elected as the chairman of the preparatory committee, and He Bingsong, Tao Baichuan, Chen Gaoyong, Sun Hanbing, Li Ximou, Fan Zhongyun, Jiang Jianbai, and Wang Xinming were elected as preparatory committee members. At the same time, the first preparatory meeting was held to discuss the simple regulations.

Simple Regulations Passed

The simple regulations passed at that time are as follows: (1) Name: Reading Advancement Association of the China Cultural Construction Association. (2) Purpose: To encourage reading, create a good learning atmosphere, and create a high cultural standard. (3) Members: (A) Anyone who is willing to read may register with the association to participate, and the methods will be determined separately. (B) Members are divided into two groups: university level and secondary school level, not limited to school students. (4) Organization: The association has several mentors, who are appointed by the China Cultural Construction Association and are responsible for guiding reading and judging grades. (5) Reading methods: (A) Every year in spring and autumn, the China Cultural Construction Association invites experts to select several types of books suitable for the above two groups, and publishes them in the newspaper. (B) After the book list is announced, those who register to read must read the books required by their group within the time limit set by the association. (C) In order to facilitate reading, the association has specially negotiated with the bookstores that publish the books to reduce the price. All members of the association can obtain a certificate of introduction from the association. (D) Anyone who participates in reading must make notes on their experience or the main points of the book at any time. In order to achieve uniformity and neatness, the note books can be purchased from the bookstore designated by the association to handle the matter on its behalf. (E) If readers have any questions about the books they have selected, they can send a letter to the mentors hired by the association for consultation. (6) Grade examination: (A) Grades are divided into two types: note grades and written test grades. The note grades account for 30%, and the written test grades account for 70% (80% of the written test questions are from the textbook, and 20% are from reference books). (B) The book list announced in the spring will be subject to a written test in October of each year, and the book list announced in the autumn will be subject to a written test in April of the following year. (7) Rewards: Divided into cash and books. All selected candidates will be given a certificate of honor, and those with excellent grades will be specially rewarded by the association. (A) University group: First place will be awarded 500 yuan in cash, second place 300 yuan, third place 200 yuan, fourth and fifth place 100 yuan each, sixth to tenth place 50 yuan each, eleventh to thirty place will be awarded a full set of books to be read in the next issue. (B) Secondary school group: First place will be awarded 300 yuan, second place 150 yuan, third place 100 yuan, fourth and fifth place 50 yuan each, sixth to tenth place 30 yuan each, eleventh to thirty place will be awarded a full set of books to be read in the next issue. (8) Supplementary Provisions: These simple regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the China Cultural Construction Association.

Reading Subjects

The reading subjects were also agreed at that time as follows: (1) Three Principles of the People, (2) Four Books, (3) Social Sciences, including political economy, law, and society, (4) History, world history, Chinese history, (5) Geography, world geography, Chinese geography, (6) Philosophy, (7) Logic. The above subjects will be read in two phases, and the phased methods will be determined separately.

Book Selection Issues

After the first preparatory meeting, a second preparatory meeting was held on the first day of this month to continue discussing various issues, such as when to start and what area will be the scope of the reading association, and the criteria for selecting books. In the end, it was decided to hire Chen Lifu, Cai Yuanpei, Li Ximou, Gao Yihan, Liu Binglin, Zhu Kezhen, Wu Xingya, and Pan Gongzhan as the book selection committee members of the reading association. Once their consent is obtained, the reading methods will be published in the newspaper, and the first phase of reading members will be solicited.

Principal Jiang Wenyu personally teaches civics. Everything has been improved. The official start of classes was on February 18th. Gold Price Falls Sharply

Reaches New Low of 845 Yuan

Plummeting a Dire 18.4 Yuan

The gold market's decline has intensified, with the downward trend showing no signs of stopping. Yesterday, a new low price of 845 yuan was seen. Observing the trend, people's confidence has been exhausted. Without any special unexpected stimulus, the future remains bleak. Early in the morning, due to the rise of silver markets in the UK and the US, large speculators were still trading above the listed price of 1875 after the market closed. The forward silver market in Montreal rose sharply by more than one cent. The price of raw gold in London rose by one shilling, resulting in frequent exchange rate contractions and cheaper pound prices. People were greatly alarmed. Trading outside the market opened, breaking the 60-yuan mark and retreating to 58-59 yuan. Unlike the previous days when the news of Minister Kung's visit to Wuhan boosted the market, those who went long have had their dreams shattered and continue to liquidate. Supply exceeded demand, falling to 52-53 yuan, and then rising to 56 yuan. People were confused, and the market was uncertain. After the market opened, Sassoon was willing to sell shillings, and the Central Bank's listing was announced, with both the UK and the US rising, and the customs gold unit falling by 1.2 cents, creating a weak situation. Yarn Prices Fall, Supported by Bullish Forces

Exchange Rates Continue to Lengthen

Foreign Yarn Prices Reasonable

Domestic Cotton Price Decline Difficult to Curb

The yarn market is generally sluggish and weak. As exchange rates rise sharply, foreign yarn prices are falling, naturally putting pressure on domestic yarn. However, a major player has organized a bullish company for standard yarn, holding firm and displaying a very strong attitude. Therefore, the current situation remains calm. However, the international flow of gold and silver is turbulent, which has a significant impact on prices in our country. Future changes are difficult to predict.

Golden Rooster: Quiet with Underlying Weakness

The opening prices of standard yarn futures for all months showed a downward trend. This was due to the sluggish overseas cotton market and the panic caused by the big "Eight Angle" gold market. Near-term contracts fell nine jiao, while far-term contracts fell seven or eight jiao. However, the goods absorbed by the bullish company remained untouched. After bidding for two or three rounds, the market tightened again. As a result, near-term contracts fell two, three, or four jiao, while far-term contracts lost seven jiao. The afternoon session opened quietly, with sluggish trading and little change in the market. At the same time, it was reported that sales of spot yarn were still sustainable. General speculators are taking a wait-and-see attitude towards standard yarn. Due to the manipulation by financially strong players, trading has decreased, waiting for opportunities to move. The closing was very stable, with each contract rising slightly by one jiao. (North Shanghai) Yesterday, 22 or 23 sources from the river arrived. The market for each good moved slightly in retail. The price of white japonica was high, and the medium-to-second grade rose slightly by five or six hao. The price of early thin indica rose by several fen, and the rest of the goods were flat.

Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

Do You Like to Eat Candy?

— Chonglou

Little friends: Do you like to eat candy? I know, you must like it very much; because the taste of "Banana Candy," "Milk Candy," and "Peanut Candy" is very good, and it feels very sweet in your mouth; but if you eat too much candy, your stomach will become sour, or you will have toothache!

Little friends: Do you like to take medicine? I know, you definitely don't like it; because the taste of "Castor Oil," "Magnesium Sulfate," and "Quinine" is very bitter, and it feels very uncomfortable in your mouth; but if you are sick and can't move in bed, the doctor gives you medicine, but it can cure your disease and restore your health to normal.

So we can't say that sugar is good because it tastes sweet, or that medicine is bad because it tastes bitter. Not only are sugar and medicine like this in the world, but there are many other things like this. For example, games are very happy and reading is very troublesome, but if a person only knows how to play games and doesn't know how to read, then his knowledge will not be built up, and he will not be able to stand in society in the future, and he will not even have a bowl of rice to eat in society! Conversely, if a person is willing to study hard and doesn't play too much, then he will definitely be able to build up a wealth of knowledge in the future and contribute a great career to society.

Little friends: After listening to my words, are you preparing to be a hardworking child or a gluttonous child?

Hoping that Children Will Also Become Inventors

— Dazhai

Little friends, seeing this title, you may say that you have read too little and are too young, how can you have such hope for me, isn't it a joke? But, it's not a joke, really, let's look at the little friends in Soviet Russia recently.

Soviet education is developed, and children also study hard, so the inventions of children have reached as many as 2,000 kinds. Looking back at our country's little friends, are there any inventions? But I have never heard of it.

Watt invented the steam engine when he was young after seeing boiling water. Ford invented the car structure when he was young after repairing watches. Using children's curiosity, creating great mechanical inventions, it can be seen that children becoming inventors has long existed in Western countries, not just starting today.

Inventors are certainly not easy to be, but what they find is in the ordinary things that everyone is used to seeing and hearing, paying attention everywhere, and examining them. It's just that they have sharp eyes, delicate brains, continuous perseverance, and a spirit of struggle, so they can see, think, and do it, so that their purpose can be achieved. It is the hard work of hard work, not the lucky success of carelessness and airiness. Little friends, if you want to be inventors, you must know that there is nothing mysterious, and usually put your strength into it. As the saying goes, "Those who have the will are also like this", it is not impossible to achieve.

How to Organize an Extracurricular Reading Club

— Shen Yanying, a 13-year-old girl from Shanghai Longhu Primary School

Extracurricular reading clubs help us increase our interest in reading and develop self-study habits.

The extracurricular books that everyone reads are different. Some like to read historical stories, some want to see funny pictures, and some like to read adventure novels. Then, those with similar interests can be grouped together to form a group. (There are six people in each group in our school)

Ask the teacher to find a way to collect the books read in each group. After we finish reading, we gather together and everyone talks about the joy of reading.

Our extracurricular reading club has various competitions. Which group reads more or faster. Report to the General Assembly once a week. Reviewed by the committee.

Dear little friends! You can also organize an extracurricular reading club, which has several benefits.

(1) Books can be exchanged with each other (be careful not to damage them.)

(2) You can ask questions that you don't understand and discuss them together.

(3) Cultivate the ability to read books by yourself.

(4) Increase all knowledge.

Okay, let's organize it!

Why Do Frogs Hibernate?

— Chengzhao

Little friends, to know "Why do frogs hibernate"? We must first study whether frogs are warm-blooded animals or cold-blooded animals?

Zoology tells us: "Whether the climate is hot or cold, the body temperature of animals remains unchanged, which is called warm-blooded animals. Otherwise, they are cold-blooded animals." When the climate is warm in summer, frogs are also warm. But when winter comes and the climate is cold, the frog's body also becomes cold. Do you think frogs are not cold-blooded animals?

Because the frog's body becomes cold when it is cold in winter; so at that time it always shrinks its limbs and can't do anything, and can't even do things like eating! It will only hide in the ground to sleep, which is called "hibernation".

Little friends, I think you must be wondering and asking me: "So frogs don't eat food during hibernation, won't they starve to death"? Yes. Because frogs can't eat food when they hibernate; so they have to eat more food in the warm summer. Like ants, these cold-blooded animals, when the climate becomes cold in winter, they hide in their nests and don't come out. But they have already accumulated food for the winter in the summer?

Animals Living a Cooperative Life in North America

— Zhu Ming

North American river beavers have very sharp teeth. They gnaw off tree trunks and take the bark and branches as food, and take the trunks as nests. They often gather the strength of the same kind and use their very sharp teeth to gnaw off the roots of the trees along the shore. When the roots are gnawed off, the tree falls into the river, and they use the fallen trees as dams; they surround the water along the river bank and store it in the dam, and all the beavers live in separate groups, like a village. The same kind are sent to serve as guards, stationed permanently, and if they encounter an enemy attack, everyone will go forward to resist together.

The bighorn sheep of Rocky Mountain also gather the same tribe into a group. If they are on the road to travel and rest, or when they are collecting food, they must take turns to be guards to protect the whole group.

The wild bison in the North American plains often travel in teams, walking in a line, often taking two or three days to complete. Therefore, some farmers and workers often encounter them, blocking them from moving forward. Also, when other tribes invade, they will put the old and young in the center of the team, and the strong on the outside of the team, and work together to resist the enemy. If a wolf snatches a cow from the herd, then those—a group of cows that have not been snatched, will work together to chase after it, and will not stop until they get the cow back.

Science Teacher Magic

— He Gongchao

Please Nose as a Detective

Science teacher was on stage again not long after the start of school. He took three copper coins and said to the audience:

"Little friends, today I will do magic, only using these three copper coins; but although there are few tools, it is still very interesting and meaningful to change. From this, we can know: If we understand all kinds of scientific common sense, then, even if they are a few copper coins or a few pieces of paper, they can be used as experimental tools and can also change into magical magic."

"Today, this magic trick needs my nose to help. Come, come, come, little friends!" He said, spreading his palms and putting three copper coins in his palms, closing his eyes, and said to a child in front of the stage:

"I'm not watching, you can take away any one of the copper coins. After a while, you return the copper coin to me, and I will ask Mr. Nose to detect which copper coin you took away, and it will be correct.—But my eyes are always closed."

The child waved a copper coin in his hand that was thinner with two five-color flags.

Science teacher said: "Put it on the side of the stage, don't hold it in your hand."

He continued to close his eyes and squeezed the remaining two copper coins tightly in his palm. After two or three minutes, he said to the little friend again:

"Now please return the copper coin you took away to me."

Now, he still has three copper coins in his hand—he put them on his nose one by one, as if asking it to smell them, and finally, he unhesitatingly held the copper coin that the little friend had taken away in his hand and showed it to the child, saying:

"It must be this one, right?"

When the child looked at it, it was indeed the thinner copper coin with two five-color flags. So everyone praised and wondered.

"It's very simple to say. It turns out that copper is a metal, and metal is a very easy thing to conduct heat. The remaining two copper coins were placed in my hand for a few minutes, and the heat from my hand was transferred to them, so they were all warm; but the copper coin that this little friend took away did not transfer heat, it is still very cold. When I touched these three copper coins one by one on the tip of my nose, because they were different in cold and heat, I knew which copper coin had been taken away. Isn't it very simple and interesting? At the same time, we can get a common sense, that is, metal is easy to conduct heat. If we use paper balls or cloth strips to experiment, this magic trick will fail, because these two things are not easy to conduct heat."

The Adventures of Sinbad the Sailor (8)

— Xin Qing

Before long, they reached the ship. We watched them climb up like monkeys, and finally they were on our deck.

They pulled down the sails and dragged the ship to the shore, but we dared not lift a hand to stop them. They made us go ashore, then left us, took our ship, and sailed to their own island.

Look at the island they abandoned us on, it was feared by people. For this reason, when it can be avoided, no ship dares to sail into it.

After those dwarfs left, we continued to walk forward, passing through the land, discovering some herbs and fruits, but we all thought we were not far from death. Finally, we saw a large house in the distance, so we set off towards it.

This was an extremely large structure, with a large black wooden door, fit for a king's residence.

We went in through the door and immediately saw a pile of human bones, and nearby were several iron forks for roasting meat, as if used by cooks to roast large pieces of meat. Seeing these things made us tremble with fear.

While we were in this state of sorrow, the door suddenly opened, and a tall, black man walked in. He was as tall as a tree; he had only one eye, right in the middle of his forehead, shining like burning coal; his mouth was huge, his hands were long and sharp; his ears were large and wide, like the ears of a large beast, and his nails were like the claws of a carnivore. When we saw this terrifying sight, we fainted and lay on the ground like dead men.

Later, we woke up and saw the black man still standing in front of us. He looked at us for a while, then walked towards us. He picked me up with both hands, caressing my whole body, but there was nothing but skin and bones on me, so he put me down. He picked up my friends one by one and caressed them in the same way.

Our leader was not as thin as the rest of us, so the black man picked him up, pierced him with an iron fork, and roasted him over the fire. After roasting him, our enemy ate him and then lay down to sleep. He slept soundly all night, his snoring loud, shaking the whole house.

You can be sure that none of us could sleep that night. When dawn came, the man woke up and went out, leaving us in the palace. After he left, we tried to find a way to kill him. When night came, we were still full of fear for our lives.

Women's Sphere

Written Before "March 8th" Festival

— Zi Jiu

The gentle spring breeze blows out tender green willow buds, the warm sunshine nurtures sprouting grass, the earth returns to spring! Even the weak willows and delicate grasses can grow freely, but the majority of women on the Chinese land still live their old-fashioned lives!

In 1907, when the earth returned to spring, Ms. Zetkin of Germany led international women to establish the International Women's Congress, engaging in the women's liberation movement and the labor movement. The congress was established on March 8th in early spring. Since then, to commemorate this meaningful event and hoping to continuously strive to achieve the final goal, it was decided that this day would be "International Women's Day."

Therefore, Women's Day is not a good festival for ladies, grandmothers, and young ladies to chat, talk, dance, gather for meals, and so on, but a memorial day for women to rise up themselves to seek liberation and happiness.

Since then, every year on this day, women from various countries have held enthusiastic commemorative meetings. However, the way of commemoration varies in its purpose due to the different positions of women in each country. Those who have already been liberated naturally celebrate with joy and dance. Those who have not yet been liberated follow the past struggles and plan future combat strategies.

Chinese women, because they have been poisoned by feudal society, live an inhuman life. Open a Chinese cultural history, and you will know that the entire Chinese society in the past was dominated by Confucianism. How did the Confucian eyes see women? Just from the simple definition in the Book of Rites: "Women follow others, in youth they follow their fathers and elder brothers, when married they follow their husbands, and when their husbands die they follow their sons," it can be understood. It clearly casts women into a subordinate position, stipulating that she has no independent and self-respecting person or behavior. Later, Song Confucianism advocated women's chastity, which further deprived women of their sexual freedom. By the end of the Ming Dynasty, the saying "A woman's lack of talent is a virtue" completely wanted to treat women as a speechless puppet.

The wheel of time finally crushed the stubborn thoughts of the Chinese people and gave birth to the New Culture Movement of the "May Fourth" era. The women's liberation movement was also one of the goals of the New Culture Movement at that time.

However, with the slowing down and lurking of the revolutionary tide, the retro style has become rampant again, re-singing the chastity of women, driving away remarried women... These are all clear evidence. We do not oppose preserving national essence, nor do we oppose maintaining inherent virtues, but the past Chinese contempt for women is a fact. Before this "March 8th" in 1935, groups engaged in the women's movement should unite to oppose feudalism and blind restoration.

At the same time, the iron hooves of imperialism are trampling on China everywhere. Chinese women should open their eyes and recognize their true colors when the earth returns to spring.

Women's Issues Lecture

— Jun Hui

Lecture 2: Biological Exploration of Gender Issues

Section 1: The Question of Gender Superiority in Biology

I think that anyone who studies women's issues must first correctly understand the question of gender superiority in biology. Because when our research takes the first step, we will encounter opponents who stand on the biological point of view and advocate male superiority to oppose gender equality. If we do not have a correct understanding of this issue, it is easy to admit male superiority and place women in a preordained inferior position.

We know that all the rulers in history have created certain principles or laws suitable for them in order to maintain their dominant position forever, so that the general ruled people believe in them and obey them! There are many such examples. The ancient Greek aristocratic philosopher Plato advocated the sacred theory of aristocracy, and King Charles I of England in the Middle Ages advocated the divine right of kings. Similarly, in a male-dominated society, the theory of male superiority will inevitably arise, which will be used as a theoretical basis to explain male dominance and even as a mysterious mantra to consolidate its dominant position! This is not surprising at all.

The so-called male superiority theory undoubtedly originated after the establishment of the so-called patriarchal system. For thousands of years until now, it has dominated the minds of all people, and regardless of whether they are male or female, noble or lowly, they regard it as a God-given theorem. Not to mention the past, even in the "civilized century" that advocates gender equality, ordinary women with unclear minds still recognize this theorem and recognize the preordained inferiority of women themselves. This is undoubtedly a major obstacle to the women's liberation movement!

So, what is the theoretical basis of the so-called male superiority theory? Its argument is first and foremost the most primitive and unscientific theory of yin and yang, for example, taking natural phenomena such as heaven, earth, sun, moon, yin, yang, water, and fire to symbolize male and female. To prove the theorem that men are superior to women, the Book of Changes says: "Heaven is superior and earth is inferior, Qian and Kun are determined!" This can be said to be the most typical symbolic argument, but today, it has lost its value! Secondly, the most important argument is biological and even physiological. According to it, all creatures take the male as the main body, and the female is only its appendage. Especially in the animal kingdom, such as mammals and birds, males are physically stronger than females, the organization of various parts of the body is also more complex, and the appearance is also better. Humans are the same. Whether they are barbarians or civilized people, women are generally shorter and weaker than men, the weight of their brains is also less than that of men, and their mental activity is also lower than that of men. In this way, women are naturally inferior to men. This is the so-called biological male superiority theory.

Those who advocate male superiority, like other mechanical phenomenalists of the rulers, only observe phenomena with a fixed eye and want to fossilize phenomena, but they are unwilling to examine the causes and essence of phenomena with a dynamic eye. The male superiority of some animals and humans is a real phenomenon, and this phenomenon must have its historical reasons! However, the discovery of this reason is the greatest threat to male dominance. Why? Because this will lose the theoretical basis of male dominance!

Modern science, especially the development of biology and sociology, has finally clarified the essence of gender issues in humans and even the biological world. Darwin discovered the law of biological evolution and shattered the ghost story of the ruler's God creating Adam and Eve; astronomer Copernicus invented the heliocentric theory and broke the traditional geocentric theory; and the author of ancient society, Morgan, discovered the matriarchal system and explained the historical causes and essence of the patriarchal system. In particular, Lesterwood, an American sociologist and biologist, invented the female-centered theory of the biological world, giving a fatal blow to the traditional male superiority theory!

According to Watt's research results, biology originally took the female as the main body, and the male was only its appendage. The female is the source of life. In the process of biological evolution, in order to make the organism more advanced, the male thing was derived from the female, so that it can fulfill the task of cross-fertilization of heterogeneity. In some humans and higher animals, there seems to be a phenomenon of male superiority, but this has its own special reasons. In human society, the general prevalence of male-centered theory is the result of superficial observation, stubborn rumors, habits, and prejudices.

Here, we see two completely opposite theories of gender issues. Namely, male-centered theory and female-centered theory. But Watt's words are based on science, and we still have to believe him. He himself said: "My research is like Copernicus' heliocentric theory and Darwin's theory of evolution, which eliminated many criticisms and shattered the rumors of the time, and will soon sweep away the male-centered theory."

Modern American Women

— Guan Lu

In the old feudal society, everything about women was not free, freedom, freedom, freedom of career, freedom of sex, and freedom of various activities. Women's labor was exploited, their sexuality was occupied; their position was subordinate, a position of slavery.

The rise of capitalism called out the slogans of equality and freedom, and advocated the women's liberation movement, reforming the imbalance of the status of men and women in the feudal era. So, what kind of life do women in capitalist society live? How do they enjoy the rights of freedom and equality? Now let us first take a look at the women in the United States.

Now the United States is the most developed capitalist country, and American women are also relatively free women in many countries; the so-called slogan of "Ladies First" that supports women's rights is also best practiced in the United States. From this point of view, American women are completely liberated, completely equal and free!

Originally, when women of the general upper class talk about freedom and gender equality, they always think that freedom is to enjoy property rights and civil rights equal to men. They regard freedom as pursuing careers, engaging in creative work, and not being hindered by gender in any occupation or career. Such freedom, in capitalist countries, is mostly already obtained by women of the privileged class. Legal obstacles and shortcomings have also been mostly deleted and revised in the United States. Many institutions of higher education and occupational positions have also been opened to women.

Moreover, in the privileged groups, housewives can hire servants to handle household affairs, and those with children can hire nannies! Or pay to send their children to private kindergartens. In this way, a married woman can comfortably engage in various careers like a single woman, and can occupy a major position in the field of occupation and career.

However, in capitalist countries, apart from these privileged classes and women with special forces, what about the general women of the middle and lower classes who rely entirely on intellectual and physical labor?

We can take a look at the general living conditions of many intellectual and physical working women in the United States:

Teachers in schools, the career of teaching in schools, in the United States in recent decades, has almost been mostly the career of women. In the past fifty years, the number of male teachers in schools has gradually decreased. According to a survey in 1930, out of the 1,037,000 teaching positions in the United States, 853,967, or even more than 80% of the people, were women. In the past ten years, the number of female teachers in the United States has increased by more than 200,000, and the number of female teachers in all public schools has exceeded three-quarters of the total. However, the remuneration for female teachers in general schools is less than that for men, while the work done is equal, which is a determined method.

Clerks in institutions, in the past ten years, the number of female clerks in various institutions in the United States has increased from 500,000 to 1,986,830. Almost half of the clerks are women.

Before the start of the economic crisis, the salaries of clerks in American institutions were relatively high. Starting in 1926, the salaries of female clerks began to be reduced. The salary of female secretaries was on average 14 yuan and 66 cents less per week than that of men. Female bookkeepers were 10 yuan and 87 cents less than men. During the crisis, salaries were generally reduced by 10 yuan to 20 yuan per week. However, the salaries of male clerks at that time were still almost twice that of women.

Waiters in hotels and restaurants, for the special working ability of women, waiters in hotels and restaurants are also mostly women. The total number of female cooks in all restaurants and hotels in the United States is 94,252. Female waiters 209,593. Other female workers 109,124. From 1900 to 1930, this number gradually increased over these thirty years. As for their salaries, they have also gradually decreased in recent years. For example, the Blackstone Hotel in Chicago used to pay cooks 12 yuan per week, and some hotels paid 15 yuan. However, after the economic crisis, in the spring of 1930, some were reduced to 30 yuan per month, while men were paid more.

Now, let's take a further look at the working women in the machine factories that are directly related to capitalist production in capitalist society:

The more developed capitalism is, the more advanced the machines are, the more skilled workers are squeezed out, and the more women and children without specialized skills are absorbed into the factory.

Before 1817, a great thinker said: "Women and children are the first thing that capitalists who master machines seek." By 1848, this great thinker and his friend had also seen that capitalism would absorb a large number of women into the production process. Because machine production does not entirely require heavy work, what capitalists need more is to use women to participate in work in light industrial plants and pay low wages.

Now let's look at the female workers in the United States. The number of female workers in general factories in the United States exceeds that of male workers, whether in spinning mills, cotton mills, or many light industrial factories. For example, the number of female workers in cigarette factories exceeds that of men by more than 74,000. In the past ten years, a total of 50,000 workers have also been laid off. The reason is that there are more female workers and the productivity is faster, so there is no need for so many workers.

I remember a person in the United States who was engaged in factory investigation saying to a factory manager: "Why do you like to recruit female workers instead of male workers?" His reply was: "For the work in light factories, female workers do it faster and better than men." Capitalists use women's ability to work hard, have patience, have no specialized skills, are easy to be controlled, can sit in the machine room all day, constantly work, constantly produce. And the results are better than male workers, so male workers are squeezed out.

As for wages, the wages of female workers are generally less than those of male workers. This is the case in many large factories in the United States. In 1933, there were many factories that hired a female worker for 1 yuan and 40 cents a day, while the male worker used to be paid 5 yuan a day. Roughly, the wages of female workers are 20% to 70% of the wages of male workers.

In capitalist society, physical working women, in addition to being excessively exploited for their labor, are often unable to develop according to their natural physiology due to the factory system, such as long working hours, night work, and other factory systems that hinder hygiene and physical development; and most adult women are prematurely aging.

Capitalism also sets regulations on working hours, factory laws to protect laborers, and calls out slogans to protect children and women, but these are only regulations, and these regulations still stand on the side of the factory owners, and laborers do not get benefits.

Looking at all the women's lives above, how do women live in capitalist society! How are the slogans of freedom, liberation, and gender equality advocated by capitalism used on women!

Women serve in society, participate in production in factories, and are not equal to men in terms of labor costs. When they return home, they naturally have a master-slave relationship between men and women due to the dominant economic position of men. In terms of gender relations, due to the commodification in capitalist society, women have also become commodities, occupied by men with economic advantages, and sexual life has become prostitution.

In the United States, although the slogan "Women First" is emphasized, this slogan is only an outer garment. In essence, due to economic dominance, the first is still the man, the husband; it is also the same as other free and equal forms of expression in capitalist society.

Based on the above situation, in capitalist society, women have obtained great opportunities in their careers; even in many schools, institutions, and other service places, the number of women exceeds that of male employees. But looking at the cost of women's labor, male and female employees who do the same work, the salary of female employees is less than that of men. Precisely because the cost of women's labor is low, schools, institutions, hotels, hospitals, and many places that need workers like to hire women. Therefore, in capitalist society, although there are many professional women, on the point of profession, the status of women is lower, and men and women are not equal.

The Life of a Buddhist Academy

— Qian

Several years ago, when I was wandering in a famous town in the Yangtze River basin, I happened to meet several female lay Buddhists who had seen through the world and become nuns to study Buddhism. They lived in a place called a Buddhist Academy. This Buddhist Academy was ideally suited for monks and nuns, built on a hillside in a secluded and quiet location. Not far from the entrance were two large vegetable gardens. Passing through a stone-paved path about ten feet long between the gardens led to the lecture hall, also known as the classroom. Further inside, a seven- or eight-foot-long corridor led to the main hall—the place for worshiping Buddha. On both sides of the main hall, connected in a row, were Chinese-style bungalows divided into front and back suites, which served as the bedrooms and study spaces for the female lay Buddhists.

There weren't many female lay Buddhists in the academy, only seven or eight in total. It was said that they were transferred from a lay Buddhist association across the river. These seven or eight female lay Buddhists were all in their early twenties and had received considerable education, some even having worked as teachers. However, if you only glanced at their bald heads, the wide gray cloth robes covering them from neck to ankle, white cloth socks, nun shoes shaped like silver ingots, and the rosary beads on their wrists, you probably wouldn't have a good impression of them. If I hadn't lived with them for a few days, I would never have imagined that behind that solemn, otherworldly demeanor, there was a heart as full of life as mine, and that their emotions were even stronger than those of ordinary people.

Their daily routine included three scheduled visits to the main hall for worship: the first at 4:30 in the morning, the second at noon, and the third at 6 in the afternoon. In the dim morning light and the dark twilight, in front of the "ancient Buddha with a green lamp" in the main hall, the female lay Buddhists' chanting, soft and continuous, mixed with the occasional sound of the big drum and the constant "po ya po ya" of the wooden fish, sounding like a plea or a lament. On weekdays, when a Dharma master or layperson—usually male—came to lecture, they also attended several classes in the morning and afternoon. The textbooks were naturally nothing more than things like "The Awakening of Faith in the Mahayana," "The Avatamsaka Sutra," and "The Diamond Sutra." When the lecture began, the eyes of the Dharma master or layperson on the platform were fixed on the scripture on the lectern, while the eyes of the female lay Buddhists below the platform were fixed on the scripture on their desks. The lecturer buried themselves in lecturing, and the listeners buried themselves in listening. Such a teaching scene, in the eyes of an outsider, was quite amusing.

These grand occasions of lecturing were not held every month, nor were they held exclusively in this Buddhist Academy. Sometimes they were held in other towns hundreds of miles away. At such times, the female lay Buddhists, like wandering monks, would wear straw sandals and travel to attend the lectures. As for their usual life in the academy, apart from going to the main hall three times a day for worship and occasionally attending lectures in the classroom, they would each copy or recite scriptures in their own rooms. In the evening, after worshiping Buddha in the main hall, they would each meditate and contemplate their own Zen. Although in this quite civilized town of the 20th century, electric lights were not available to them, Cao Xueqin's poem could still be used to describe them: "Pitiful are the daughters of noble families, sleeping alone beside the ancient Buddha with a green lamp." In their remaining free time, they would sew and wash their own clothes and socks, or each think their own thoughts.

In this kind of place for monks and nuns, the private property system has not yet been eliminated, and it can even be said that its existence is greatly encouraged. The status of the female lay Buddhists in the eyes of the manager (a cunning woman in her forties who had taken vows but not left the household) was directly proportional to their own private property. The Buddhist Academy had the obligation to provide the female lay Buddhists with clothing and food, but the female lay Buddhists had the obligation to perform rituals and chant sutras for the academy's patrons. Sometimes, when wealthy old men died, their wealthy sons or wives wanted to do something special, so they would invite these female lay Buddhists to chant sutras in the inner courtyard in the middle of the night, their silver bell-like voices resonating inside and out. This seemed like the final romantic service to the deceased. Sometimes, when the distinguished fathers or mothers of high officials, dignitaries, or famous and wealthy people passed away, the head of the academy would issue an order, and the female lay Buddhists would be led by the manager to the deceased's mourning hall, reciting scriptures day after day to help the deceased's soul transcend. Sometimes, this would continue for forty-nine days. By the time the female lay Buddhists' voices were hoarse, the head of the academy's pockets were full—not to mention the number of people who used their names to solicit donations outside on weekdays. This kind of life, I think, the female lay Buddhists never dreamed of when they shaved their heads!

I know in detail the reasons why four female lay Buddhists became nuns. Three of them were very close sisters in their secular families. Because they were all dissatisfied with their marriages, when the eldest sister's wedding date approached, the three of them quietly escaped to a convent in a neighboring town and shaved their heads. The fourth, a quite wealthy lay Buddhist, became a nun because her wealthy fiancé already had two concubines before marrying her as his legal wife, so she left home in anger. Now, although women are not as unfree in marriage as they used to be, in this era of endless chaste women, filial daughters, heroic women, and virtuous women, when customs are becoming increasingly antiquated, I think that soon, some married women who are dissatisfied with their marriages or are abused will also adopt this slow form of suicide to gain fame and praise. In that case, will my old acquaintance from a few years ago, the desolate Buddhist Academy in a certain famous town, soon have "flourishing business extending in all directions"?

Women of Baoding

— Zigang

Open the map of Hebei Province and we can find the three towns that form a triangle: Beijing, Tianjin, and Baoding.

It used to be called Baoding Prefecture, but now it has been changed to Qingyuan County. There was a period when it became a military stronghold and was relatively prosperous for a while. However, Baoding's most prosperous period was when Cao Kun lived there, because important people came and went, and large-scale hostels appeared—two of them—before disappearing without a trace.

Although Baoding once had a prominent history, women here have not experienced much development.

The women here still retain the simple characteristics of the countryside. This flavor is already quite strong in Baoding city, but it can be even more confirmed when you go to the four villages around Baoding. All the fashionable novelties cannot be found here. The new women that people generally pay attention to are just the female students in middle school. They are all dressed in plain white tops and black skirts, going to the streets on holidays to buy some school supplies or daily necessities. This is their most frequent opportunity to contact the outside world. Due to the female students' serious and simple style, people also treat them with a harmless attitude. Newspapers rarely use female students to find topics for amusement, a situation that is not easy for us to find in other cities.

As for love, it is simply a rare thing in Baoding's student circles, because firstly, boys and girls attend separate schools, and secondly, most of the students come from the countryside. Under the early marriage system, the students who come to middle school are already men with wives and women with husbands. Therefore, their private lives are stable. The highest institutions of learning for female students are Baoding Women's Normal School and Women's Vocational School. Their way out is to become elementary school teachers or to seek further education and work in other counties.

The general urban women are still considered diligent and thrifty. Apart from a few who manage their homes, are addicted to mahjong or gambling, and cannot talk about economic independence, most still cannot do without men's support. They earn a little pocket money in their spare time by sewing, because there are several sock factories in Baoding, so hemming the tops and mouths of socks has become a common occupation for women. This is done by taking materials from the factory and doing it at home, without having to go to the factory to work.

The rural women in the four villages are more able to support themselves. Like men, they have strong arms and great strength, and can spin thread and weave cloth in their homes in addition to working in the fields from dawn to dusk. However, in recent years, because weaving cloth from yarn spun by crude wooden machines would result in losses, the clumsy local tools finally could not compete with the dumping of foreign goods, and most women have given up this occupation and are now using foreign thread to weave cloth.

What is most prominent in the four villages is the child bride system. This custom is extremely common, even more so in the last two years. Because the poorer they are, the more they want to send out their young daughters who are "going to be someone else's family sooner or later" as child brides, saving food. On the other hand, they are also poor and cannot afford to hire long-term workers or buy livestock, so they hope to adopt child brides early to help, using them like livestock. Without exception, the lives of child brides are forever without sunshine. When they first arrive at their in-laws' home, they only have half a month of novelty—that is, for only half a month everyone treats her as a newcomer, not starting the brutal labor life yet. After this period, they are not polite. The newcomer is already busy in the cowshed and in the fields. In addition to labor, they also suffer unreasonable beatings. The so-called one generation pays for another. The mother-in-law always remembers the pain she suffered when she was a daughter-in-law. When she becomes a mother-in-law, she must repay the principal with interest. This is all due to the lack of knowledge. Also for this reason, child brides very much hope to have sons and marry daughters-in-law, because following these stages, their own pain can be gradually reduced.

This is a microcosm of the women of Baoding. Whether in the city or in the countryside, there are still more dark sides. Let's investigate the reasons.

Please do not worry.

Amateur Chat

The Standard of Beauty

— Wang Yiming

From the perspective of general absolutists, things that are beautiful are beautiful regardless of the era, society, or people. They say that Yang Guifei would still be an undeniable beauty in modern times, so the standard of beauty is absolute. However, the problem is not that simple. In fact, the characteristics of beauties in the feudal era were "three-inch golden lotuses" and "willow waists," while the modern "standard beauty" is one who bares her chest, highlights her breasts, and uses a pair of natural feet to support her swaying body. Therefore, even Yang Guifei with her "three-inch golden lotuses" and "willow waist," I think, would not be recognized as an absolute "standard beauty" in present-day Shanghai, except perhaps as an antique to be appreciated. At the same time, the views on beauty differ from society to society and from group to group. In our view, the decoration of Indian women is the ugliest. They wear lantern-style pants, wrap their heads, and some even clamp metal objects on their noses. It is really extremely ugly, but Indians think this is very beautiful! We say that African Americans are too black and not good-looking, but they are afraid that they are not black enough, and often apply black things to their faces to make them black and shiny to show their beauty! Furthermore, if you put an old-fashioned portrait of a beauty next to a modern nude painting, and then ask a young artist with neatly combed hair and a farmer from the countryside to evaluate them, then I dare say that the conclusions they reach will be very different. All of this fully illustrates that the views on beauty in different eras, societies, and groups are not absolutely the same. In this sense, we can say that the standard of beauty is relative, not absolute.

However, on the other hand, although the views on beauty differ from group to group, the views on beauty are the same within the same group. Although there are various different views on beauty in the same era and society, that is, the views on beauty of various groups exist, there must be one view on beauty that occupies a dominant position in this middle ground. This dominant view on beauty is the standard of beauty in that era and society. In the feudal era, the magnificent architecture, the great and sublime statues of gods, and even the yellow robes worn by emperors were the preferences of the feudal aristocracy, but these preferences dominated their era, and therefore those things became the publicly recognized beautiful things of that era and society. Similarly, tall, smooth-faced Western-style houses are the architecture of the wealthy, but at the same time, they are also considered beautiful architectural art by modern people, because this kind of aesthetic tendency dominates this era. Therefore, although a standard of beauty that transcends eras and societies cannot be established, there is a certain standard of beauty in the same era and society. In this sense, we can also say that the standard of beauty also has its absolute meaning, and is not absolutely relative. The view that the standard of beauty is absolutely relative is another erroneous manifestation of absolutists.

Fundamentally speaking, human aesthetic concepts do not come from innate talent, but are formed in their social life. The reason why the aesthetic concepts of people in different eras, societies, and groups are different is because their lives are different, not because they are born with different aesthetic concepts. Why do feudal aristocrats consider magnificent architecture and sublime and great statues of gods to be beautiful? That is because these things easily evoke a sense of solemnity and respect at first glance; they are very beneficial in maintaining their authority. Why do farmers like healthy beauties and dislike "delicate" beauties? That is also because they have to work, and a healthy beauty is helpful to their lives and does not add burden. If the problem is shifted to the decoration of the general ladies of the current city, then it becomes even clearer. You know, the decorations of modern cities change so quickly that new decorations appear almost every year and every month. If you make the most fashionable clothes this year, it may become "old-fashioned" next year. The year 1935 has not yet passed, but Chinese and foreign clothing stores, car dealerships, and department stores have all come up with new styles and new signs for 1936. Two years ago, fashionable girls loved to wear long stockings, but later they wore short socks, and now they don't even wear socks, simply showing off their physical beauty. In terms of coats, short coats were popular two years ago, but the so-called new style coats recently are long and dragging, and even have slits in the back. ... What is the reason for this? My answer is: modern urban life is extremely unstable and is constantly changing. Those who are tired of material life and those who cannot find a way out in this changing life and feel distressed are increasingly seeking new miracles and new stimuli. The manifestation of this situation in art is the sudden appearance and disappearance of those so-called new trends such as Dadaism, Cubism, Fauvism, and New Sensationalism. At the same time, the rapid and ever-changing new decorative styles are also a reflection of this situation. Therefore, finally speaking, the standard of beauty is determined by the human way of life; the so-called relativity and absoluteness of the standard of beauty can only find a practical basis in human life.

Of course, saying this does not mean that everything that is useful to human life can be called beautiful. No, this is a wrong view of pragmatists. In fact, kerosene is useful to us, but it is not beautiful; manure is also useful to farmers in the countryside, but they do not recognize it as beautiful; ... Therefore, we can only say that all beautiful concepts are the products of human real life, and all standards of beauty are determined by human life, but we cannot say that everything that is useful to human life can be called beautiful: perhaps we can say that all beautiful things are practical, but we cannot therefore say that everything practical is beautiful.

Training and Cultivation

On Willpower

— Manqian

Willpower (Will) is what expresses a person's strength.

When things come to a head, whether you will succumb or whether you will "give up halfway" depends entirely on whether your will is strong. There are many opportunities that can give your future great hope, but hesitation and procrastination, without any determination, cause those opportunities to drift away. I have also seen many young people who, because they cannot overcome the environment, finally fall under the enormous force of the environment. This is proof that they lack strong will.

Only through willpower can judgment be born. However, for willpower to be able to make correct judgments, it must pass through the net of reason. Only by using willpower extremely rationally can extremely correct judgments be made.

"Stubbornness" and strong willpower are two completely different things. Stubbornness may be a prejudice that is biased towards emotion, and it is often just a "preconceived notion." It is an internal traitor to the success of a person's career, ruining more than succeeding!

The highest realm of strong willpower is: being incorruptible by power and unmoved by poverty. For example, a master wants to harm his enemy and finds his servant. The conditions the master offers to his servant for committing the crime are high position, much money, and beautiful maids. How should the servant deal with this current problem under such a serious order and bewitching temptation? This requires him to bring out his inherent "willpower" to see whether willpower gains the final victory or whether the lure of material things gains the final victory.

So, how to use willpower? I say: first, you must have an indomitable spirit; second, you must be confident; and third, you must be deep and resolute. I will explain them separately below:

First, you must have an indomitable spirit. If you have already carefully decided on your will, you must do your best to promote it. "The head can be cut off, but the will cannot be bent"; "Success or failure, profit or loss, is not considered." You must know that any undertaking will never be without resistance; and the truly successful undertaking must first eliminate resistance or transform resistance into assistance. If a supervisor sees a strong enemy in front of him and does not inspire the morale of the army, it is unlikely that he will not fall into personal ruin and disgrace. He must first put the army in a position of no retreat, and then the officers and soldiers of the three armies can embrace the determination to break the cauldrons and sink the boats, and only advance and not retreat. The thing called willpower must be adhered to without change.

Second, be confident. For the steps that you have decided on, there is absolutely no room for turning back. People with talent have strong willpower, and their confidence must also be strong.

Columbus firmly believed in the theory that the earth is round, and people thought he was absurd and ignorant,

Page 20

but driven by his self-confidence, the American continent was finally discovered by this person with strong will, who did not change because of the satire of customs.

Third, be deep and resolute. People cannot be without emotions, but the use of emotions must not exceed a certain limit. Otherwise, it is like an unbridled horse, running wild without end and impossible to control. Therefore, before handling matters, one must first adopt an extremely rational attitude, analyze calmly, and never allow emotions to act on temporary impulses. You cannot allow emotional impulses to ruin your future. You need to develop an attitude of "depth, resolution" and "restraint."

Industry Surveys

Silk Industry

— Yi An

According to the foreign trade reports of the Jianghai Customs over the years, silk and tea have always held the top positions in export trade. However, since 1928, while the tea industry has been able to barely maintain itself amidst constant losses, the golden age of the silk industry has become a relic of history!

Now that the silk industry is barely clinging to life, it should be meaningful to discuss the organizational situation of the silk industry in Shanghai, right?

In Shanghai, there are as many as 116 silk filature factories that meet modern mechanical reeling standards. Most of them are located in Zhabei and Nanshi, with less than 20% located in the concessions. Before 1928, it was the golden age of the silk industry. As soon as we stepped onto the edge of Datong Road in Zhabei, we could hear the thunderous sound of machinery shaking our eardrums. Each towering chimney spewed thick, foggy smoke, which filled the entire sky over Zhabei. From this interwoven scene of rattling machinery and pervasive smoke, everyone thought that the future of the silk industry was paved with a golden avenue. However, the reality before our eyes tells us that the silk industry has reached its final moment of twilight. What we will see in the future are more and more silk factories with court seals on their doors.

In the past, the huge capital power that held these 116 silk factories was mainly from the Wuxi and Suzhou groups, and the Huzhou group also accounted for a significant portion. The late wealthy merchants Hu Xueyan and Xue Runsheng were even giants in the silk industry. These former owners of the silk factories, who were once prominent in the silk industry, have either passed away or could not withstand the impact of the crazy economic depression, thus losing the courage to continue operating. As a result, the silk factories in Shanghai disappeared one by one like the morning stars at dawn. Now, only less than twenty factories are struggling to operate. Moreover, although these fewer than twenty factories are running, they are like sailing ships in a stormy sea, with the danger of capsizing at any time.

Speaking of the reasons for the silk industry's disastrous defeat, many people attribute it to their loose organization, lack of scientific management methods, and obsolete machinery, leading to low production efficiency and other problems. In fact, anyone familiar with the inside story of silk factories will deeply understand that these are still secondary issues. Because the organizational situation of general silk factories is not much different from other factories. If there is any difference, it is only because of the different production methods that there are slight differences from other types of factories.

The general organizational structure of a silk factory is similar to that of an ordinary yarn factory. Above the factory is a management office, which is in charge of all matters of the factory and all external powers. The interior of the management office is roughly divided into four departments: general affairs, business, cashier, and warehouse. The factory has a factory director, engineers, and foremen. All affairs of the factory are directly responsible to the management office by the factory director, and all male and female workers in the factory are subject to the control of the factory director.

Among these various positions with different responsibilities, the one with the greatest power and the most complex affairs is the "General Affairs" department. The daily salary of a general affairs director, generally speaking, can earn between 20 to 40 or 60 yuan. Next, the "Business" director, this is a talent who must have rich experience in the silk industry's commerce to be competent, but in terms of affairs, he is much more leisurely than the "General Affairs" director, so the remuneration he receives from the factory is not much different from the general affairs director. As for the position of factory director, it is very different. He must not only have very rich experience in the silk industry, but also be a technical talent who can actually work with his hands. He is responsible for all affairs of the factory, and in terms of production, he must have the skills to improve products like an engineer. Therefore, the factory's generous treatment of him is not inferior to that of the general manager of the entire company. Engineers are only specialized positions, and the highest remuneration will probably not exceed 100 yuan. However, in addition to receiving generous salaries, these many senior staff members also receive a large "bonus" at the end of the year, which ordinary workers dare not expect.

The workers' work is divided into departments by the factory in advance. The work of a general silk factory is roughly divided into the following types: workshop, silk room, reeling room, cocoon peeling room, and silk floss room. The number of people working in a workshop generally accounts for 70% of the total number of employees, and some workshops even have more than that. Secondly, the number of workers in the silk floss room and the reeling room accounts for an average of about 10% of the total. The work in the workshop can be individually divided into three types: long line, substitute line, and basin filling. The work of basin filling is entirely done by child laborers, with only one child laborer used for two machines. Long line is one person per machine. This type of work is mostly done by girls who are sixteen or seventeen years old to be qualified for this better-paid position. Substitute line cannot be regarded as a formal work department, because the purpose of this type of work is only to prepare for workers who are absent from the long line, and then replace them to work. Therefore, there is sometimes no fixed number of people doing this type of work.

Generally speaking, the work on the long line is much more difficult than other departments. From the raw cocoons entering the pot, through the intermediate processes of silk reeling, distinguishing the quality of the silk, the size of the reeled silk, and the grade of the color, all these procedures that require sufficient brain power to do well must be done one by one by the workers in charge of the long line. Naturally, a long line worker's possession of this ability cannot be achieved overnight. An ordinary long line worker must receive at least three years of training to graduate.

The work in the silk room is also done by female workers. This type of work is very easy, but the task is conversely very important. The work in the silk room can be divided into two parts: joining ends and reeling silk. The work of joining ends is to take the rough silk picked out by the male workers, and then have them remove the rough silk and still connect the silk ends together. This procedure of joining ends is considered successful. The work of reeling silk is even easier and simpler. You only need to reel the strands of silk into a form similar to "crispy hair flowers" to complete the procedure of reeling silk. As for saying that their responsibility is important, that is because the final inspection procedure when a package of silk is packed is also handled by them.

The work of reeling silk is also not something that ordinary people can do happily. This requires picking out the cocoons of countless cocoons, selecting the quality of the cocoons, and listing the grades of the first, second, and third classes separately. But the work of cocoon peeling room and silk floss room is much easier. The work of cocoon peeling is a type of work that uses finger strength. You only need to peel off the outer shell of the cocoon to complete a procedure. Silk floss room is not suitable for unhealthy women. Because the silk floss has to go through a series of knocking, washing, and loosening procedures, if women with weak wrists, simply cannot be competent.

Among these many department's works, the best treatment is for workers on the long line. Because they can also be regarded as a kind of specialized technical talent among ordinary workers. Their daily wages are about 36 cents to 60 cents, and the most will not exceed one yuan. But recently, the wages are only between 30 cents and 40 cents, and there is no way to imagine the former generous income. The work of silk room and reeling room workers also only cost five to seven cents a day in the past. Now, they can only calculate half of the original number. As for the wages of cocoon peeling room and silk floss room workers, it is a kind of activity wage calculated according to the goods. A skilled female worker can earn up to about of dollars a day. A novice female worker, that simply can't be said to be wages, the result of working non-stop all day, roughly can earn about 200 wen a day.
