Amateur Cafe

Freedom and Necessity

— De Chong

Is human consciousness and behavior free, or is it limited by necessity? This has always been one of the most important issues of debate in the ideological world. According to general religious people and idealists, human consciousness and behavior are absolutely free and are not subject to any restrictions. They say: Man is the spirit of all things, and human consciousness can control everything and create everything. You see, are not all civilizations and all systems created by man? However, where does the consciousness and behavior of the person who creates everything come from? General religious people and idealists cannot scientifically and actively attribute it to talent, and finally hand over the solution of the problem to the mysterious God. In fact, human consciousness is formed in the environment in which it lives, and its behavior is even more regulated by the consciousness formed by this living environment. People in primitive times were subject to natural constraints anytime and anywhere because their production tools were very primitive, and they were slaves of nature. Therefore, they could only fight ferocious beasts in groups, and could only "eat raw meat and drink blood" to fill their stomachs, and "live in caves" to settle down. It is absolutely impossible to have the mentality and consciousness of living in a western-style house and eating a big meal, so they cannot have the action of making these things. In the past, in China's primitive agricultural society, people's lives were completely dependent on primitive agriculture. If that year was "good weather for the crops" and a good harvest was obtained, then they could live a better life, otherwise there was a risk of starvation. Therefore, at that time, the Chinese people could only place all their hopes on God, praying for "good weather for the crops" and a good harvest, and they would never have the consciousness and behavior of using scientific methods to make rain or using electricity to cultivate fields. Although in all the past Chinese fairy tales, there were Taoists who could call wind and rain, and immortals who could fly into the sky and escape into the earth, but this was just a kind of mysterious thought produced by people at this time when they felt the magic of nature but could not understand it, not a real thing. Therefore, our opinion is exactly the opposite of that of general religious people and idealists. We believe that human consciousness and behavior are not free, but are necessarily regulated by nature and society. People who live in a certain natural and social environment will inevitably have certain consciousness and behavior, and cannot have other consciousness and behavior. In this regard, human beings are slaves of nature and society, and their consciousness and behavior are not free, but are restricted by necessity.

However, people not only live in accordance with the environment, but also can change the environment to make their lives better and better. If people can only adapt to the environment and be slaves of nature and society, and cannot change and overcome them, then there is no such thing as human evolution. The evolution of human society is the result of human beings constantly fighting against nature and society. However, human beings' changing society and conquering nature are carried out under their understanding of the necessity of nature and society. The extent to which human beings can change society and conquer nature depends on the extent to which they recognize the necessity of nature and society. Within a certain time and space, if people can understand the necessity of nature and society, then they can freely deal with them under this understanding, and thus change from slaves of nature and society to their masters, and their consciousness and behavior can also be said to be free. For example, when we do not understand the necessity of water, we are helpless when we encounter the vast ocean. Conversely, if we understand everything about water, and thus know that ships will not sink on the water and can move freely, then we can take a boat on the water, and the vast river will not limit us. Here we can be said to be free. For example, in the era when feudal society was about to collapse and capitalist society was about to be born, if we did not know the necessity of social development and tried hard to uphold feudal society, then we would be like a mouse drilling into a cow's horn, the more we drill, the tighter it becomes, and eventually we would be pushed into the grave by the necessity of social development. Conversely, if we recognize the necessity of this society and thus determine our actions, then we will become the masters who lead society forward, and in this regard, we are free. Therefore, Hegel believed that "freedom is the insight of necessity." Engels also said: "Freedom is nothing but the domination of ourselves and external nature, based on the understanding of the necessity of nature. So freedom is necessarily a product of historical development." Because people can increasingly recognize the essence of objective things and understand their necessity, in the development of history, people can dominate necessity based on their understanding of this necessity, which is freedom.

At the same time, within a certain time and space, we dominate this necessity by recognizing the necessity of social development, and practically promote the development of society, making this necessity a reality. In the meantime, we become the masters of necessity because we recognize it, and thus gain freedom, and then practically promote the development of society under this recognition. Here, our recognition and practice become the main conditions for the progress of history, and freedom is transformed into necessity.

Therefore, freedom and necessity are not absolutely opposed to each other. We must correctly understand their contradictory and unified relationship in order to correctly determine our actions. If we only pay attention to the necessity of objective things, and think that under this necessity, human beings can only let everything grow naturally and have no way to do anything, then we are useless fatalists. Conversely, if we ignore this objective necessity and only believe in human creativity, thinking that human power can absolutely overcome nature, then we are unrealistic utopianists. Both are wrong. We must understand objective necessity and then dominate it in order to promote the development of society: such a correct understanding of the relationship between freedom and necessity to determine our attitude towards life and to determine our behavior.

We know that in primitive times, human beings were slaves of nature. Later, with the development of society and with human beings' understanding of the necessity of nature, human beings are gradually overcoming nature and dominating nature. By modern times, because of the development of industry and the invention of science, human beings are even more able to dominate the necessity of nature by understanding it. Now it can be said that nature has no major obstacles to human beings, and the so-called people who are slaves of nature have gradually become the masters of nature. However, even now, social relations still have great pressure on human beings, and human beings are still slaves of social relations. Therefore, if human beings want to obtain complete freedom, they must reform or improve this social relation in order to shorten the leap from the "kingdom of necessity to the kingdom of freedom."

Scientific Talks

Human Anatomy

— Qi Ming

Man, this is an animal that is neither big nor small. To say that he is small, then the microorganisms under the microscope, the single-celled protozoa, Amoeba, etc., are unknown how many times smaller than him. To say that he is big? Then he is several to tens of times smaller than the giant elephants in the tropical rainforests; if compared with the whales, the giant beasts in the sea, he is even more tens or hundreds of times smaller. Because the weight of a person is probably only around sixty or seventy catties to one hundred catties, while a whale weighs thousands or tens of thousands of catties. However, although man is just a medium-sized animal that is neither big nor small, the expression of his intelligent spiritual life has always become a mysterious mystery for philosophers to explore. Many idealistic philosophers regard human reason as a sacred gift, believing that this is not a kind of ability that the material world can possess, but a special expression of divinity. For example, Plato had long believed that man lives between the world of God and the world of form and matter, his body falls into the turbid material world, and his spirit belongs to the world of God. At the time when Darwin's theory of evolution came out, Wallace still insisted that the human spirit was an injection of spirituality. Even the modern scientist Thomson still said that the human spirit was suddenly discovered. Of course, the French encyclopedists of the 18th century have always firmly believed that the human spirit is like his body, based on natural matter, and his spirit is the manifestation of the functional expression of his material organization that is different from other animals.

Continued on page five

Common Sense

On Common Sense About Common Sense

— Tan Ran

"You don't even have enough common sense, are you worthy of meddling in this matter?"

Such words are used by people in many places as a conclusive reprimand to others, which shows the importance of common sense in daily life. So, what exactly is "common sense"?

Regarding the question of "what is awareness," if studied according to a scientific system, there would naturally be very rich explanations of the theories and materials regarding the "common sense" question. However, since our readers are reading articles during their "spare time," we must find a way to start with the most clear and simple phenomena to raise questions about "common sense." Now, let us first tell a story:

Not long ago, there was an agricultural Ph.D. who had studied abroad and returned to his country. He was proficient in agricultural management and familiar with various agricultural technologies. He ran from a foreign country to his hometown—Gansu Province—and first invited several friends who were enthusiastic about business to raise hundreds of thousands of dollars to buy dozens of acres of fertile land. He also spent more than one hundred thousand dollars to purchase several sets of electric tillage machines and harvesters from Europe. In addition, he ordered hundreds of thousands of dollars' worth of fertilizer and seeds. After hiring hundreds of farmers, a new-style farm was quickly built. However, after a year, the agricultural Ph.D.'s business suddenly went bankrupt.

Friends all said that the agricultural Ph.D. had "bad luck," and the local villagers also discussed, saying that the agricultural Ph.D.'s "using foreign goods" was "selling out the country," so the result was naturally to be "condemned by Heaven and Earth."

In this matter, we can get good material. We first discovered here that the agricultural Ph.D.'s determination to actively carry out his business before the event was entirely due to his in-depth study of agricultural knowledge, and he resolutely carried out his plan with his extremely scientific agricultural "common sense." But his failure was not because his agricultural knowledge was insufficient. The problem was that his social and economic "common sense" was insufficient. Because the cost of his agricultural products was made up of fertilizer and part of the machine cost, it was higher than the products of ordinary local small farmers. Moreover, his large number of products could not be sold in Gansu for a while, and no one dared to bid at an excessive price. Therefore, he had to transport the products out of the province. However, the freight out of the province was extremely high. As a result, he had to hire laborers to transport thousands of piculs of grain to Shaanxi, but no buyers came to appreciate them. Finally, the capital turnover was not working, and the new-style farm had to collapse in the backward environment. In this experience, we clearly know that this agricultural Ph.D. can only serve as a technician in an advanced country with developed transportation and an unusually specialized social economy, and it is most appropriate for his specialized knowledge to guide the new-style farm. Because the "common sense" needed in that kind of environment is exactly the knowledge that this agricultural Ph.D. is familiar with. On the contrary, the reason why the small businesses operated by farmers in Gansu do not collapse but instead surpass the agricultural Ph.D.'s business is precisely because their "common sense" is suitable for that kind of environment. However, precisely because these "old folks" only understand the local phenomena of social life, and they lack scientific knowledge of the national economy and foreign technology or economics, they assert that the agricultural Ph.D.'s "using foreign goods" and "selling out the country" must be "condemned by Heaven and Earth." This is again because of insufficient "common sense." Because the judgment of "condemned by Heaven and Earth" is derived from the "superstitious concepts" of the old folks. Moreover, the agricultural Ph.D.'s "using foreign goods" is not for consumption, but for production. Logically, there is no "selling out the country." From this point of view, it can be seen that "old folks" only have "common sense" suitable for backward local farming, and their correct concepts of "repelling foreign goods" and anti-imperialism are hundreds of thousands of miles away. Their lack of "common sense" is exactly in line with the superstitious concept of "condemned by Heaven and Earth."

The interest given to us by such a story is that the lack of "common sense" or its failure to become widespread will inevitably make people confused and wandering in the complex and vast human society. If we can carefully pay attention to many daily events similar to this, we can almost always encounter people struggling in the suffering of insufficient or non-universal "common sense." What is the reason for this? Can "common sense" be made available to everyone? Under what circumstances can "common sense" be fully applied without omission?

To answer the above questions, of course, a few words will not be enough. Among the components of these questions, on the one hand, it contains the issue of the degree of human knowledge. And all research on common sense issues is inseparable from the scientific and universal education work in the process of human practice. In this short article, we can only put forward the following standards:

First, correct "common sense" should be allowed by science. "Common sense" should take the elimination of superstition as a necessary condition for its establishment.

Second, the methods and phenomena repeatedly manifested in daily life, such as clothing, food, housing, and transportation, do not belong to "common sense," they are the subject of habit. "Common sense" is a constituent of the simple cause-and-effect relationship in the complex phenomena and essence of things in the world. But it is not a specialized science, because the accuracy of science is established in continuous evolution. Therefore, "common sense" is only the knowledge that science has already solved. It is a tool that people need when they come into contact with phenomena on a daily basis.

Third, common sense does not belong to local specialized knowledge. People are often satisfied with their own specialized academic research, that is, they are confident that they have "sufficient common sense" and ridicule those who have not learned their specialized knowledge as lacking common sense. This is bound to fail. It is as erroneous as recognizing that such figures cannot become scholars without "mastering the encyclopedia." Therefore, we believe that "common sense" is the totality of various sciences universally dissolved in phenomena. Human "common sense" is directly proportional to the degree of social and scientific development.

Page 22

Page 23

. But they still dare not admit that humans evolved from natural matter, and that the spirit is also produced in that way. Therefore, they are still revolving in the theory of human nature that has been pre-existing in the universe for a long time. Regarding the human spirit, modern new philosophy has correctly recognized it in philosophy, that is, it recognizes that it is the product of long-term natural evolution, just like the human body, and there is no spirit without a material body. But right here, because practical sciences such as physiology, psychology, etc., have not yet reached a very refined, perfect, and sufficient explanation of the general mental state of people, those purely empirical scientists are still hesitant at this juncture and dare not resolutely deny the supernatural essence of the human spirit. Then, in the anatomy of man, how should we recognize this part of his mental phenomena? From the perspective of pure natural nature, the spirit must be attached to matter to exist, and thought cannot but have a physical brain first. Therefore, human spirit and reason are not the injection of spirituality or spiritual objects that suddenly change, but the result of the special functional expression of the special organization of matter that has been naturally evolving for a long time. If someone asks whether this argument is correct, then we can ask him to recall that people who have their heads cut off cannot only not think again, not become philosophers, scientific images, or moralists, but also cannot continue to survive? This is common sense, but this common sense is the scientific understanding of the mental phenomena of human anatomy, which is more correct than any theory of idealism.

The spiritual phenomena expressed by the organizational function of human natural matter are indeed very mysterious and worthy of surprise. In fact, its physical occurrence, development, and organization are equally amazing. The beginning of mankind is only a kind of reproductive cell. This kind of reproductive cell is called sperm in men and ovum in women. These can only be seen under a microscope. Such a large and ingenious thing as a human being has grown from that invisible small body, which has been clearly studied by modern science. Human sperm is only about one-fiftieth of an inch long in its entirety, that is to say, the original seed of human beings is only a small insect about one-fiftieth of an inch long. The sperm's ability to move is 3.6 millimeters per minute. Although it can live in the vas deferens for two or three months, it can only live for about ten days in the female body if it does not combine with the egg. The ability of human beings to produce sperm is very amazing. They can produce 126.25 million per week, and release 200 million to 300 million during each sexual intercourse. After the sperm and egg combine, they form a fertilized cell. This cell separates from one to two, from two to four, from four to eight to sixteen continuously in the mother's body, forming various human organs. The entire body of a person probably has more than 400 trillion cells when calculated in adulthood. The speed of its development in the mother's body, based on 280 days of fetal life, must be at least an average of 900 billion per day, which is an amazing number! As for the metabolism of these cells and how their division distinguishes the various organs of division of labor, these are specialized problems in physiology, so let's not talk about it. What we still need to talk about here is that cells are the unit of human body organization, but cells are not the ultimate quality. They are composed of molecules, and molecules are composed of atoms. I vaguely remember reading in a book that the atoms in the human body have a number as large as ten to the seventy-second power. This number is very difficult to write down on paper, so the complexity of the human body can be imagined. Indeed, if we regard each atom as a solar system, because electrons revolve around the nucleus, then the human body is composed of several solar systems that are more complex than the Milky Way in the sky. We try to close our eyes and think, we can imagine that people are an infinite group of flywheels, suspended there to stir and rotate, and can also be compared to a beautiful cosmic spectacle. However, what about between electrons and electrons, atoms and atoms, molecules and molecules? Then there are many gaps. If these electrons and atoms are squeezed into a pile, then a person who is four or five feet tall can become a small meatball the size of an egg. Such a strange human body organization expresses its spiritual phenomena through physical and chemical actions. Therefore, if it is said that spiritual phenomena are mysterious and amazing, then is its organizational state not equally amazing? Biological and cosmic material phenomena, man is the most subtle secret to the extreme. No wonder man can be called the spirit of all things.

Miscellaneous Works

Between Grandfather and Grandson

— Shi Ying

The cold wind howls in the winter.

At noon, the sunlight shines gently on the village.

A-hua lies peacefully by the bamboo fence gate, squinting her eyes. Wei-cheng and his old grandfather are also next to the woodpile, facing the sun for warmth; the old man with the white beard on his beard is over eighty years old, although his spirit is still vigorous, but the bronze forehead has been engraved with the marks of wind and frost, he is wearing a bloated old cotton-padded jacket, the indigo color has faded to white, and he is also tied with a blue as a skirt around his waist, and the white hair on his temples comes out from the felt hat with holes.

The old man's cough and choking closely followed; his face was flushed, until tears and snot flowed on his cheeks, and then he breathed a sigh of relief and wiped away the tears with his skirt.

——It's no good, people have lived long enough! Wei-cheng, I can't wait for you to graduate, I'm afraid I'll be gone long ago.

When the young man heard these words, he was really a little sentimental, and his heart was as desolate as winter. He said in his mouth:

——Grandpa, isn't it next summer?

But what the old man thought of was nothing more than what old people should think of: he narrowed his eyes and saw the young man who had grown up in front of him, with a strong and sturdy body, and an elegant and handsome appearance, which made the old man feel satisfied, ——Thirty years of painstaking expectation have finally yielded the harvest in front of him, although only the grandfather and grandson are left in the family. ——But in the end, he felt insufficient because of another thing. He regretted sending his grandson to school, isn't A-xi in the East Village the same age as Wei-cheng? A-xi's father is a grandfather with three grandsons. But Wei-cheng went to school and became strange, always saying that he would not graduate from the imperial examinations.

The old man's thoughts made him silent.

Wei-cheng knew what his grandfather was thinking about again. He ran into the hall, took a drawing board, ran back to his grandfather who was still in thought, and said to his grandfather:

——Grandpa, sit for a while. When the sun is good, I will paint a portrait for Grandpa.

——Alas, you students only know how to do these things!

When he said this, he agreed in part. Leaving his appearance to future generations is indeed a wish of the elderly, but the old man's greatest wish is to have a joyful and lively time again before he dies, hoping that his granddaughter-in-law will enter the house as soon as possible, and see them in pairs.

The wishes of the elderly are obviously a century apart from those of the young.

The young man was concentrating on the foot-width, facing the old man in front of him, and leaning over, using delicate strokes to draw on the paper.

The cold wind in late winter is just right. The sun leaked from the treetops into the shade, and the weather became extremely gloomy. The old man couldn't stand the cold before the sunset, and coughed more frequently.

A-hua stretched her waist and walked away by herself.

Biography of Celebrities

Biography of Einstein (6)

— Cong Mu

(5)

Einstein became a professor at the Kiliqi Institute of Technology in the autumn of 1912. Later, in the spring of 1914, he moved to Berlin. Therefore, much of what is said above happened after he moved to Berlin.

In Kiliqi, he was a full professor. The invitation to Berlin was to treat him as a full member of Preeson and a professor at the University of Berlin, with the same treatment as a full university professor. Before he arrived in Berlin, the Dutch chemist Van't Hoff, a professor at the University of Berlin, passed away in 1911, and he filled the position of this chemist; at the same time, he was also persuaded to serve as the director of the Physics Department of the Zhafeier Aim Institute. Such a position has always been given to the elders in the academic world, but at this time Einstein was only thirty-five or six years old, which was entirely due to the efforts of Blanck, Lalenster, etc. to recommend him.

At that time, universities in various parts of Germany were developing their own ways to compete for academic hegemony, but Berlin, as the center of German culture, still occupied a very important position. Now, with the addition of two major scientists, Blanck and Einstein, it can certainly be boasted, especially in physics. At this time, Einstein, who was in Berlin, separated from his wife who had married in Bern, and married his cousin, Airosha, who had loved each other since childhood.

Einstein's research on the general theory of relativity was carried out in Kiliqi in 1913. After 1914, it was continued in Berlin, and it was not completed until 1915 and 1916; after that, his research went further into the issue of cosmology. The results of these studies were mainly published in the Academic Senate of Preeson. In the meantime, the theory of light quanta was also a long-cherished problem for him. In 1917, in his paper "On the Quantum Theory of Radiation," based on the atomic model of Bohr, he used the leap of electrons from orbit to orbit to explain the divergence and absorption of radiation, and regarded the leap as a natural situation in the radiation phenomenon. Here, he introduced the idea of "confidence rate," and based on statistical equilibrium, he elicited Planck's law. This creative idea gave a very important meaning to the development of quantum theory; and based on the observation of the total solar eclipse by British astronomers on May 29, 1919, after the announcement in London on November 6 of the same year, the principle of relativity and the name of Einstein were publicized in the world. (To be continued)

Yao Xiao'an, Wang Pingqiu, Qilin Bao

Zhongxi (1040) 11:00 PM to 12:00 AM

Opening Piece "Naked Legs"

The ways of the world are thin and talk of strange forms. Foreign strange costumes appear in various colors. But only see hundreds of flowers and butterflies turning new styles. How many enchanting beauties dress like Sister-in-law Ting. But if those exotic beauties still dislike being ugly. One by one, naked bodies in light shirts as the typical model. Saying that promoting fitness is appropriate. Bare legs and high heels in the public courtyard. Swaying with great beauty all over the street. Causing those young masters to be like flies drawn to rotten meat. Like a vase of roses. Red, gorgeous, fragrant to the bone. A thunderbolt once issued an order. Banning the strange form of bound feet. Which resolute heroine. Put forward an article to make a sensation and listen. There are disinterested onlookers. Mixing fried snails to make a muddle. Ever since the authorities got angry. Regardless of noble ladies, thousands of gold, and little stars. Not only are bound feet difficult to walk. Men and women must also walk separately. If not obeying the instruction and defying it. Then teach you to be thrown in front of the hall to taste corporal punishment. His heart is a piece of Bodhi thought. To rectify the licentious customs and awaken dreams. At present, several provinces along the river are obeying the command. Returning to the past, the people's spirit is pure. Only living on the Spring Shen River. Still have bound feet rampant. In vain, the authorities spent a lot of effort.

Shen Bao Local Supplement - Film Special

A Brief History of the Development of Film (6) (Continued from January 11)

— Wen Ying

(6) A Glimpse of Actors' Adventures in the Pioneering Era

The previous article briefly described "A Brief History of the Development of Film." Previously, there were five paragraphs disclosed in this journal (January 7 to 11 of this year). This is the sixth paragraph. In the five paragraphs mentioned earlier, the first paragraph talked about how film audiences, from the earliest period, were the masters who created the film industry. Now, the reason why the film industry has become one of the six major enterprises in the United States, and occupies a very important position in world art, culture, education, and many other aspects, is all due to the fact that our audiences are happy to spend money to watch and enthusiastically promote it. The second paragraph talks about how a Leland Stanford, in order to prove that a horse's four hooves are in the air when galloping at extreme speed, spent several years of effort to invent the linking of films, as well as the joint photography of many camera boxes, and further developed the fantasy of continuously shooting several films with one camera box. The third paragraph is about the great inventor Edison and his deputy Dickson, working hard on this fantasy, leading to the invention of the "animated peep show," as well as the grand occasion when the first animated film, "The Great Train Robbery," was released to the public. The fourth paragraph talks about the origin and rise of the "star system," as well as the first appearance of film queen Mary Pickford. The fifth paragraph talks about how the rise of the star system was due to the audience's worship of stars, as well as the hypocrisy of the publicity work at that time. After the fifth paragraph, due to the original text not being complete, the publication was temporarily suspended. Now, the original text is continued and will continue to be continued.

At that time, the spirit of adventure of several actresses was rarely seen in modern times, so we can mention it in passing. At that time, there was a female star named Alice Joyce. She was originally a supporting actress in stage plays. When she had nothing to do, she would work as an artist's model. Because the salary in the film industry was higher, she really wanted to enter the film industry. She fabricated a story, saying that she was good at riding, no less than a Kentucky jockey. The film company hired her because there was a shortage of female riders at that time. When it came time to shoot the scene, she was placed on the back of a horse and told to gallop forward in the middle of the railway track, capturing the dangerous situation of the train chasing the horse from behind. Alice had never ridden a horse once in her life, but how she did not fall to her death, nor was crushed to death by the train, even she herself was confused. But from then on, her position in the film industry was also stable.

The glamorous big star Gloria Swanson was also very adventurous at the beginning, holding her life in her hands to make movies. In one of Cecil B. DeMille's old films, there was a scene that imitated a famous painting, "The Lion's Wife." Although the scene was very short, the heroine had to walk into the lion's cage, sleep with the lion, and have the lion put its paws on her shoulders in a friendly manner. Of course, they could not be without considerable preparation. So, the side of the cage was filled with people holding rifles, aiming at the lion. However, Gloria herself also understood that if the lion bit her head off in one bite, it would be useless even if they killed the lion. Moreover, when many gun barrels were fired at the same time, it was difficult to guarantee that she herself would not be shot.

But at that time, Gloria was very daring. Besides, everyone praised her as an incomparably brave woman, so how could she be timid and retreat, ruining her reputation. She drilled into the lion's cage in this drunken state and started filming. Fortunately, everything went smoothly, but unfortunately, the camera had a temporary problem. When Gloria jumped out of the cage, the director told her, "Sorry, the scene just now was not shot well. Please do it again." This time, Gloria was so angry that she fainted.

Entering the cage for the second time was the most difficult thing Gloria had ever done in her life. Before entering the cage for the first time, the mental intoxication had already dissipated. That kind of courage was difficult to muster again. She already deeply understood that kind of cold danger. But she had to risk her life and walk into the lion's cage again. When she came out of the cage, she was almost so nervous that she had to be carried to the dressing room. On her shoulders were the lion's claw marks, and the beads on her clothes were crushed and embedded in her tender skin.

This kind of thing will not happen now. In this place, they can use a stunt double. At that time, they could not think of any other way except to risk their own lives. Katherine Williams was also a heroine who shot beast films at that time. She also held her life in her hands to make movies. Perhaps in that pioneering era, everyone, like the people of ancient times, was braver than the average person today. (To be continued)

A Dog in "The Barretts of Wimpole Street" Earns 50 Yuan per Week

— Fu

"The Barretts of Wimpole Street," which was shown at the Nanjing Grand Theater last year, was a collaboration between three major stars, Norma Shearer, Fredric March, and Charles Laughton. People who have seen it probably have not forgotten it. What is especially unforgettable is that dog. His name is Flush. Now I will briefly talk about some of his deeds.

He is a yellow and white Spaniel, born on October 7, 1931. His owner bought him to teach him how to hunt, but his owner later said: (The distance between his two ears is too wide, it is a pity to use him for hunting). That is to say, his brain is too rich, and there is quite a bit of meaning in calling him to make movies.

Flush was selected by the film company from 75 dogs of the same species, because his eyes are full of expression, and his ears are particularly long! The hair hangs down, as bright as silk. Before the movie started shooting, he was trained by a trainer for one and a half months. The trainer said that in his many years of experience, he is the best at understanding people's intentions.

During the training period, the trainer lived and slept with the dog, personally fed him, and gained his complete trust. His nature is quiet and does not like noise. The trainer taught him to move according to the instructions of the symbols. When training him to walk on the street, he used a 60-foot rope, called him to stand at one end, and the trainer slowly pulled the rope, and the dog slowly followed the end of the rope. After walking, he had a piece of milk cake to eat. He climbed the door because the trainer called him inside the door. He peered downstairs from the top of the stairs because the trainer drew his attention downstairs. But the performance came across as if he understood the plot.

Flush had to practice for several days for each scene he acted in. If the scene of that scene was in use, he would be given the same scene. The trainer was very careful not to teach him several skills at the same time, for fear of confusing his thoughts.

Flush and Norma Shearer had already become good friends. When she was filming Rip-Tide, he followed her around, and when Norma Shearer sat down, he jumped on her. In "The Barretts of Wimpole Street," they maintained their friendship.

But Charles Laughton could not develop a friendship with him. Because in the film, he is a strict father, and the dog is afraid of him and hates him. So when filming, from beginning to end, the dog walked past him and never looked at him. Moreover, in the film, Charles's loud voice and stern scolding made the dog feel resentful. But when Norma cried, the dog felt infinite sadness. When she laughed, the dog was also very happy.

Laughably, Flush is very dignified, and walks as regularly as an old pastor. He never asks for food. That may be because he is the head of the family. He has five children in his family. He earns a salary of 50 yuan per week, but he does not have to take care of the family, because the five children have been adopted by big stars.

"Mutiny" Snippets

— Zhi Shui

Director Frank Tuttle, who has a unique and creative style, has directed three MGM blockbusters, namely "The Thin Man" (this famous film was the first to successfully change the style of detective films, and it is said that it will be re-released at the Lido soon), "Eskimo," and "Forsaking All Others." "Forsaking All Others" was the first collaboration between Joan Crawford, Clark Gable, and Robert Montgomery. Now, these three silver screen lovers are coming back with a vengeance. Under Frank Tuttle's direction, they are filming the most cutting-edge romantic comedy of a love triangle in 1935.

There are five female stars in Hollywood whose decorations often lead the fashion in the United States. They are Joan Crawford, Norma Shearer, Greta Garbo, Constance Bennett, and Carole Lombard. But among the five beauties, Joan is the most outstanding, because her beauty can fully represent the model of modern women, so not only are men fascinated by Joan, but women also recognize her as the only angel.

The technique of background and color matching has a great relationship to the overall light and mood of the film. If it is not too dark, it is too bright. Too dark, of course, will cause viewers to feel unpleasant, but too bright will feel chaotic and dazzling. For example, in "The Barretts of Wimpole Street," the eighteenth-century historical background undoubtedly makes people think of a bleak and less exciting scene. However, the artist's skillful hand has made up for this shortcoming after all, and in "Mutiny," the use of various yellow, green, and coral-colored flower papers in our country reflects the infinite sense of relaxed, bright, lively, and beautiful pleasure. It can be seen that everything depends on human effort.

The wedding dress worn by Joan Crawford when she plays the bride is called the 1935 bride's style dress. It is an oval drooping edge, a rose stamen edge, and an apron, with a swirling wind and snow-like attitude. Even the veil is a handsome product. It is short in the front and long in the back, very beautiful. At the same time, a total of 62,400 pots of cornflowers were used in the auspicious ceremony.

Chatting about "Willow Spring Breeze"

— Guo Cheng

Fred Astaire and Ginger Rogers have previously co-starred in the great song and dance film "The Gay Divorcee," which we have already evaluated. Their new film "Willow Spring Breeze"! It has now been transported to Shanghai.

This is a quite noteworthy song and dance comedy blockbuster. In addition to many stage stars showing their faces in this film, the director is still the song and dance director of the previous "The Gay Divorcee."

We are already familiar with Fred Astaire and Ginger Rogers, so here I want to talk specifically about the news about the 150 beautiful dancers. These 150 beautiful girls! All have undergone rigorous training in song and dance and are prepared to be used in the French Doll dance scene of Willow Spring Breeze. But because people feel that the girls' thighs are no longer very valuable, they hope that they can use their fingers instead of their feet to dance in slight movements.

Under such requirements, only sixteen dancers were accepted as qualified. It is really because using fingers instead of feet to dance is much more difficult than dancing on one foot.

"Willow Spring Breeze" is not worth noting for this point. It offers us many of the latest dance poses and 1935-style social dance poses, etc., which are very worthy of being taken as reference. In particular, the many songs composed by five famous arrangers that appear in the film are also worth mentioning.

Major Reform of Electric Sound Weekly

The Electric Sound Film Picture Weekly, which has been published for four years, has detailed news and photos about the secrets, undercurrents, and scandals of Chinese and foreign films in a week. Now it is heard that the ninth issue of the fourth volume of the publication will be further improved, with major reforms and enriched content. The cover will be printed in three-color version. Beautiful and pleasing to the eye. The price remains the same. It is heard that the eighth issue of the fourth volume has been published yesterday. The content is rich. Each copy is sold for only five cents.

Reader's Letters

Editor:

Previously, I was entrusted to publish the announcement of our company's sound film "Orchid in the Empty Valley" giving away songs. After the announcement was published, due to the large number of readers of your newspaper and the success of "Orchid in the Empty Valley" at the box office, the number of letters requesting songs has been five or six hundred per day, and it is still endless. Now the 20,000 copies of printed songs have been completely given away. I am writing a special letter to ask Mr. to publish an announcement to readers that the distribution of the "Orchid in the Empty Valley" songs will be stopped immediately. Please do not send any more letters to request them. I am very grateful!

Sincerely,

Film Novel

Schoolchild's Kind Mother (Grand Old Girl) (7)

— Shu Min

Sandy drove for a while and suddenly stopped the car. He said to Gilly, who was pouting, "There's something I've wanted to give you for a long time." After he finished speaking, he didn't give her a chance to defend herself, grabbed her and threw her on his lap, and spanked her butt hard. Gilly was beaten by him, and beaten very hard, and couldn't help crying. Strangely, her crying was not out of anger, nor did she feel wronged, nor was it because of the pain. She realized that this time she had gone too far. Miss Belles had repeatedly warned her before not to go too far. At that time, she disagreed and said, "If I go too far, it won't hinder anyone else. At most, I'll harm myself!" But now she had harmed Miss Belles, and it was too late for her to regret it.

Gilly was spanked and obediently sat next to Sandy, returning to the city in silence. Sandy didn't speak for a long time either, but this silence had a different taste. Although he was afraid for Miss Belles's future, he had a new hope for Gilly's future.

The next day, Joseph Jerai convened an education meeting. In that meeting, everyone silently listened to his speech: "She used to ridicule us arbitrarily... She ate the public's salary and should educate children, not treat children as her experimental products... Therefore, I request... not request, I demand... that this old outrageous principal be dismissed... This is the only way to protect the reputation of our clean society!"

Lula Belles walked out of her school as usual, wanting to go home. She walked past the door of the "front room" and couldn't help but sigh, looking inside it was pitch black. Her efforts, her money, were all in vain. And on that door, there was a sign nailed, with the words "Education Bureau Sealed" written on it, which was her fatal wound. She looked at it and couldn't help but feel sad. Just at this moment, she saw Clarence Dade standing in front of the house across the street. Not wanting to show weakness, she forced a smile as if nothing had happened and said to Clarence, "Clarence, you have won again. You have defeated Arfontel again. I have been conquered by you..."

But Clarence Dade did not look gloating. He thought that this old woman really had some backbone and couldn't help but feel admiration in his heart. So he said, "I was just thinking... maybe you didn't do anything wrong... maybe I can also earn this money by selling ice cream alone... maybe..." He stared at her, feeling really unbearable. He continued, "I was thinking... I want to take over the "front room" and use it as a legitimate business. From now on, there will be no more "back room."" He looked at her with hope, and also with some self-reproaching bitter smile. Lula Belles couldn't help but say happily, "Clarence, you are really a good person. I feel like this is meaningful, no matter what happens."

They were talking lively when a truck passed in front of them, and a bundle of newspapers was thrown off the truck. Dade caught it casually, took out a newspaper, looked at it and said, "No matter what we become in the future, at least one of your students has a promising future." As he spoke, he pointed out the news in the newspaper to her. She took a look, and it said in large headlines: "The President is not coming to Arfontel." The smaller words below were: "The head of state issued a declaration on American foreign policy, shocking the world; although it is only about twenty miles away, he has no time to visit his hometown." They read that news and smiled at each other. Dade said, "Think about it, he was most shy when he was a child, and we gave him a nickname, called Little Girl. His words can now shock the world! I think you have at least some credit for this shocking thing?" Belles also laughed and said, "I wonder if when he is giving a speech now and forgets his sentences, someone is reminding him from the side." But Dade silently stared at that newspaper, and the smile on his face also disappeared. Miss Belles quickly asked, "What's the matter?" (To be continued)
